  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText8642937024848323845" style="display:none">This is the way the world ends... for the last time.<br /><br />The season of endings grows darker as civilization fades into the long cold night. Alabaster Tenring – madman, world-crusher, savior – has returned with a mission: to train his successor, Essun, and thus seal the fate of the Stillness forever.<br /><br />It continues with a lost daughter, found by the enemy.<br /><br />It continues with the obelisks, and an ancient mystery converging on answers at last.<br /><br />The Stillness is the wall which stands against the flow of tradition, the spark of hope long buried under the thickening ashfall.         if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

        $('edition_28118494').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_28118494').hasClassName('ignored')) {

<a href="/questions/1050261-how-did-nassun-know-about-the-word">How did Nassun know about the word &quot;magic&quot;? Wasn&#39;t it introduced by Alabaster during a private talk with Essun?</a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/28376561-quentin-lucas">Quentin Lucas</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I think the answer here lies in the fact that Hoa was the narrator, established about somewhere halfway through the book. And he, in his apparent omni<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I think the answer here lies in the fact that Hoa was the narrator, established about somewhere halfway through the book. And he, in his apparent omniscience (I guess because he's a stone eater?), knew of the word and its importance to Essan, and occasionally used it to describe the adventure's of Nassun. But I don't think (though I could certainly be wrong) that Nassun actually spoke the word herself. <br /><a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1920158-laura"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1562855058i/1920158._UX100_CR0,38,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1920158-laura">Laura</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I do believe that Hoa wants the Moon back in its orbit around earth, which would appease Earth and bring life back to what it once was before the Seas<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I do believe that Hoa wants the Moon back in its orbit around earth, which would appease Earth and bring life back to what it once was before the Seasons. On the other hand, Steel/Gray Stone Eater wants to bring the Moon completely back to Earth--colliding the two and killing all humans (possibly Earth and the Stone Eaters, too). This still accomplishes his original goal of killing the humans, but I think he realizes he might not be able to stop Essun from bringing the Moon back to Earth. <br /><br />That's what I gathered from his last passage:<br />"It will be a terrible thing. It will end the Seasons. It will end <i>every</i> seaon. And yet . . . what you're feeling right now, you need never feel again. No one will ever suffer again." <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1783986608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783986608" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1783986608?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316229265" href="/book/show/28118494-the-obelisk-gate">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1783986608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13687037264280420047"><b>2.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>Buddy read with the lovely <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063711531?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melanie!</a></i><br/><br/><b>The Obelisk Gate just won the Hugo Award 2017 for Best Novel of the year category, and coincidentally, I finished reading the book on the same day the result of the award was announced. Sadly, it’s not a happy coincidence because I highly disagree with it.</b><br/><br/>This is probably the most unpopular opinion I ever wrote so far. At the time of posting this review, out of 12470 ratings, less than 200 readers rated this book below 3 stars, I am one of them. I lo</span>
  <span id="freeText13687037264280420047" style="display:none"><b>2.5/5 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>Buddy read with the lovely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063711531?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Melanie!</a></i><br /><br /><b>The Obelisk Gate just won the Hugo Award 2017 for Best Novel of the year category, and coincidentally, I finished reading the book on the same day the result of the award was announced. Sadly, it’s not a happy coincidence because I highly disagree with it.</b><br /><br />This is probably the most unpopular opinion I ever wrote so far. At the time of posting this review, out of 12470 ratings, less than 200 readers rated this book below 3 stars, I am one of them. I loved The Fifth Season, very much. It’s a work of a genius and I gave it 4.5 stars. Believe me when I say that I truly wish I could love this book the same way but I just can’t. I am severely disappointed with it and as usual, I will always be honest with my ratings and reviews regardless of the majority’s opinions, so here it is.<br /><br /><b>To summarize my mixed feelings about this book, The Obelisk Gate is majorly inflicted with the infamous second book syndrome.</b> For reasons I can’t mention to avoid spoilers, I’ll just say that the first book has the advantage of being fresh in every element Jemisin implemented and in my opinion, she failed to live up to it. It’s not a surprise, I knew right after finishing the first book that the second book won’t be as good, but I just didn’t expect it to be this much.<br /><br />Told only from two main POV and one minor POV, Essun’s POV is where I had tons of problems with. Within the first 70% of the book, her story is heavily filled with tons of info dump fired off at rapid succession, and I know I’ll forget most of them within a week after reading. Some of them are interesting for sure, but I was mindlessly bored reading her POV. Few revelations to the story aside, there’s nothing interesting out of Essun’s POV this time for me, her character doesn’t develop much, she resides only in one location throughout the whole book, and admittedly I actually fell asleep reading her story and had to force myself reading through it. When some actions did appear in the end, the damage has been done and I can’t bring myself to care anymore towards anything that happens in her story at this point because of how stagnant her character development has been compared to before.<br /><br />The other major problems I had with the book this time lies within Essun’s second person present tense narrative. In the first book, it’s understandable to use this choice of narration for her POV, I feel like there’s no reason to use it again in the second book, can’t tell you why for spoiler reasons again. Plus, in the first book, the story was told from three main POV’s switching back and forth equally, with the other two characters done in third person perspective narration, Essun’s narration style didn’t felt as distracting, instead it felt fresh to go back to because there was enough break between her and the other characters chapter. In here, there are only two main POV, reading Essun’s second person present tense perspective style in heavy dose is really something I can’t tolerate.<br /> <br />It’s not all bad of course because I thoroughly enjoyed reading the other main POV. To make my review completely spoiler-free, I won’t even mention the name of this character but the storyline that was told from this character is amazing. Full of character developments; deal with tons of Xenophobia topic, and also, in my opinion, the most important aspect in preparation for the third book. This character also shed some light and complexity to Schaffa’s character. Another positive part of the book is that the world-building is still great. The Stillness is a post-apocalyptic setting done right in high fantasy. Basically, the other main POV and the world-building are the only factors that stopped me from DNFing this book. <br /><br /><b>That said, I will continue to read the Stone Sky because everything in this book is truly a setup for the final installment and I’m still intrigued to find out how it all ends.</b> However, even if the third book ended up being something I thoroughly enjoyed like The Fifth Season, I know this is a trilogy that I won’t be rereading again in the future. All opinions are based only on my experience, the high chances are that you’ll have a different experience from me, and I sincerely hope that you love this more than me. I am basically on a lonely island screaming “I don’t like this book” to Spongebob and Patrick right now.<br /> <br /><i>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/26-pat-reviews/727-theobeliskgate" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13687037264280420047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1734169356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1734169356" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1734169356?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1734169356" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3720974336371101739">Edit 8/11/17<br/><br/>HUGO WINNER for 2017!!!!! That's the second one in a row for the SAME series! :) And since I've already read the third one and squealed all over it, I'm going on a limb and calling it three Hugos in a row.<br/><br/>Don't hate me if I'm right! :)<br/><br/><br/>Original review:<br/><br/>My mind cannot stop dancing with joy after reading this. You might say that I'm dancing with Father Earth, enjoying the reveals as one would enjoy the unearthing of so many gems of storytelling awesomeness.<br/><br/>The world-building is still sha</span>
  <span id="freeText3720974336371101739" style="display:none">Edit 8/11/17<br /><br />HUGO WINNER for 2017!!!!! That's the second one in a row for the SAME series! :) And since I've already read the third one and squealed all over it, I'm going on a limb and calling it three Hugos in a row.<br /><br />Don't hate me if I'm right! :)<br /><br /><br />Original review:<br /><br />My mind cannot stop dancing with joy after reading this. You might say that I'm dancing with Father Earth, enjoying the reveals as one would enjoy the unearthing of so many gems of storytelling awesomeness.<br /><br />The world-building is still sharp as ever, and so many questions have answers in this second book. We're given an amazing shape for amazing things to come. I'm not merely or only shaken to my core by the amazing scenes of earth alteration, depth of histories, or revealed enormity of what is really going on, here; actually, I'm left in awe by the scope and the careful planning and execution of the Author's Mad Skillz.<br /><br />Essun and Nassun are wonderful characters, of course, and there are times when Nassun almost steals the spotlight for me, but here's the real surprise: I can't believe how awesome Hoa's story is turning out to be, or that of all the Stone Eaters. This is what SF designed for. Awe. Shocking audacity. Scope and Vision. Rocking Ideas. <br /><br />So we're descending further than geological processes, headed straight into the quantum loam. :) I'm laughing my head off with Alabaster's thrown bone when he describes the spaces between atoms, the networking forces, as "Magic". :) <br /><br />Of course, any sufficiently advanced technology that allows men and women to become effectively immortal and not constrained by matter is Magic, right, Stone Eaters? lol<br /><br />Essun continues to transform even more than her previous love, Alabaster, and it's a deep process that's nearly continental in it's impact, but that's where most of my love is going. Nassun's transformation into one hell of an anti-hero nearly matches how much appreciation I have for Schaffa's changes. I sympathize for everyone, and no one is disappointing. :)<br /><br />The final action in this book is dark, that's for certain, but even now I can't stop grinning and being so damn awed by what happened.<br /><br />This is why I read. This is why I'm a fanboy. This BLOWS ME AWAY. :) <br /><br />Hell, this stuff is the stuff of LIFE. :) Totally Awesome! <br /><br />Book 2? It may not be as mind-altering as the first, but together, they're something much greater than their parts. :) Now how in hell will I be able to wait for book 3 to find out what happens to the moon? This is breathtaking in conception. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3720974336371101739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2063711531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063711531" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2063711531?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063711531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10153058274681960798">1.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567118098' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fifth Season</a> ★★★★★<br/><br/>Buddy Read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783986608?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Petrik</a> ❤<br/><br/>I finished this book just after it won its Hugo award for the best novel of 2017. This and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567118098' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fifth Season</a> are so deserving of the awards and praise they receive. These books leave me wordless, because there is no explaining how much of a meaningful impact these books have on the world, let alone the SFF community. All I can truly say is thank you to N.K. Jemisin for this world, these characters, and these important messages that continue to ren</span>
  <span id="freeText10153058274681960798" style="display:none">1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567118098" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> ★★★★★<br><br>Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783986608?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Petrik</a> ❤<br><br>I finished this book just after it won its Hugo award for the best novel of 2017. This and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567118098" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> are so deserving of the awards and praise they receive. These books leave me wordless, because there is no explaining how much of a meaningful impact these books have on the world, let alone the SFF community. All I can truly say is thank you to N.K. Jemisin for this world, these characters, and these important messages that continue to render me speechless. <br><br>I also finished this book the same night that white supremacists rallied at Charlottesville and spread their hate in my country. The country that says we are past racism. The country that is constantly telling us that we are the greatest and most forward-thinking country of all time. The country that’s passing this hatred and violence off as “free speech”. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But if you stay, no part of this comm gets to decide that any part of this comm is expendable. No voting on who gets to be people.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Literature does represent our real life. <i>The Broken Earth</i> trilogy makes us feel the things it does because it mimics our world today. It shows us the oppression unapologetically, and this oppression doesn’t just live in this SFF book, it’s in our world right now, even if you’re choosing to keep your eyes closed to it. This series is a masterpiece and I hope you read it, but I also hope you learn from it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502573489i/23572200._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Obelisk Gate</i> picks up where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567118098" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> left off, where earth’s civilization is beginning to prepare for a new Season. What doesn’t kill them quickly, will starve them to death slowly. This book mostly follows Essun, one of the most powerful Orogene in existence, where she is trying to live in a new community in a rather strange location. She meets up with old friends who are now also a part of this community, but her thoughts never stray from her daughter that has been missing since the start of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567118098" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a>. Essun is also met with new problems and dilemmas that are so much bigger than the community she is residing in. <br><br>This is one of the most immersive books I’ve ever read. The narrative of this book just forcefully will pull the reader into this broken world, regardless of if they want to or not. You can’t help all the connections you will feel and form subconsciously. You end up with this experience that just feels so real and so emotionally overwhelming. Plus, I read this with so many tears in my eyes constantly, because even though this earth is trying to kill everyone that inhabits it, it is still the humans that are the terrifying villains. <br><br>Also, this is the most beautifully crafted diverse cast I’ve ever read in any piece of literature. The representation is just on an entirely differently level. And I believe with my whole heart that every other author out there should aspire to seamlessly create their cast of characters like N.K. Jemisin. <br><br>On top of the amazing diversity and representation, as a woman, I really sympathize with the underlying theme of motherhood throughout this series. I do not currently have any children, but I’d one day like to, and this book just emphasizes that there is no word to describe the love a mother feels for her child/children. Like, this book is heartbreakingly beautiful, and this constant reminder of how it feels to lose a child is something I can’t put into words. I think that is every parents’ greatest fear and this book doesn’t shy away from that topic ever. The heart of this novel is oppression, but the soul of this novel is that there is nothing a parent wouldn’t do to protect their child.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You serve a higher purpose, little one. Not any single man’s desire—not even mine. You were not made for such petty things.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But this all being said, this book does feel like the second book in a series, and it feels like it’s leading up to what I’m sure will be a perfect ending in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2068625584" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stone Sky</a>. There wasn’t any filler so to speak, but the events very slowly unraveling to put the pieces in place so that everything makes sense. But please, don’t let that stop you from giving this once in a lifetime series a try. It truly is a masterpiece that deserves all the praise and hype that is bestowed upon it. <br><br>And speaking of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2068625584" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stone Sky</a>, I don’t think my body, heart, or soul is ready for this eventual reunion. Yet, I don’t think anything is going to stop me from devouring this book while I’m 35,000 feet in the air come this Tuesday! <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10153058274681960798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1632000694" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632000694" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632000694?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=diverse-reads-2017">diverse-reads-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632000694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9173679078649007161"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490599182i/22325551._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>▐ <b>WINNER OF THE HUGO AWARDS 2017 for best novel</b>▐<br/><br/><b><u>4.5 stars</u>.</b> I see you. <i>"I can't stand Fantasy novels! They're all the same! There are too many characters! It's predictable! Unrealistic! Not diverse!"</i> ← Trust me, I hear you. <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26228034-the-obelisk-gate' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Obelisk Gate</a> is different, though, and here's why you should give it a chance :</b><br/><br/>① 
  <b>You're very tired of reading the same uninspired writing over and over again? Fear no more!</b>
 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2917917.N_K_Jemisin' rel='nofollow noopener'>N.K. Jemisin</a>'s writing is nothing short of <strong>fantastic</strong>, with perhaps the best second Person POV I'</span>
  <span id="freeText9173679078649007161" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490599182i/22325551._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>▐ <b>WINNER OF THE HUGO AWARDS 2017 for best novel</b>▐<br><br><b><u>4.5 stars</u>.</b> I see you. <i>"I can't stand Fantasy novels! They're all the same! There are too many characters! It's predictable! Unrealistic! Not diverse!"</i> ← Trust me, I hear you. <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26228034-the-obelisk-gate" rel="nofollow noopener">The Obelisk Gate</a> is different, though, and here's why you should give it a chance :</b><br><br>① 
  <b>You're very tired of reading the same uninspired writing over and over again? Fear no more!</b>
 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2917917.N_K_Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">N.K. Jemisin</a>'s writing is nothing short of <strong>fantastic</strong>, with perhaps the best second Person POV I've ever read. Indeed she manages to master it so well that we almost forget how rare that is. Sure, I've been a little worried after the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852-the-fifth-season" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a>, given that the narrator's identity was spoiled at this time. Yet it made the experience even better for me in the sequel, especially because we got snippets of what this character was feeling, and well... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I love his stone ass, okay? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>② 
  <b>You can't stand the sight of these same white, cis, abled, male main characters that Fantasy books force down our throat 99% of the time. Fear no more!</b>
 I've already praised it in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852-the-fifth-season" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a>, but it's rare enough to repeat it endlessly : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2917917.N_K_Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">N.K. Jemisin</a>'s world is SO diverse, I love it. Several characters are POC (including the female lead), there is a polyamorous relationship in book 1, a disabled main character, an F/F romance... I'm sure I forget some, but what you need to know is this : <b>the world created by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2917917.N_K_Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">N.K. Jemisin</a> is diverse, and hence realistic.</b> Way to prove how ridiculous it is to think that a full white/cis/straight/etc cast is possible. That's called laziness.<br><br>③ 
  <b>You've not been awed by a magic system since forever, mostly because they all sound the same, one way or another (they really are). Fear no more!</b>
 I've read two books in this series now, and I still want to learn more about orogeny, because I find the concept fascinating. Not to mention that the winks to the real world - and environment issues - make it even better.<br><br>④ 
  <b>You've read 30% of <em>The Fantasy Book</em> and again, you already know how the fucking book will end because hey! You've read it before! Fear no more!</b>
 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26228034-the-obelisk-gate" rel="nofollow noopener">The Obelisk Gate</a> offers such an intricate and captivating plot that you won't be bored one second. Trust me. <strong>PAGE TURNER ALERT.</strong><br><br>⑤ <b>If you hate Fantasy casts more often than not, complaining that there are way too many characters to remember, chance are... you're just not reading great Fantasy novels.</b> Indeed what make them insufferable is not the number of characters in my opinion, but the thing that we can't separate them because they all sound the same and don't bring anything more to the story. If every fucking one is flat and unable to interest you, I feel your pain, truly. Fear no more! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26228034-the-obelisk-gate" rel="nofollow noopener">The Obelisk Gate</a> brings well-rounded secondary characters to life and pictures multi-layered MC I LOVED. Not to mention the amazing characters dynamics that feel so <i>real</i> and moved me something fierce.<br><br>⑥ 
  <strong>HOA. I WILL PROTECT HIM WITH MY LIFE OKAY.</strong>
 Sure, I already liked him in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852-the-fifth-season" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a>, but he hit me right in the feels in this one and honestly I'm so emotional just rereading quotes, it's not even funny.<br><br>Now the real question is : <strong>what are you waiting for? Start this series already.</strong><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1904631795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904631795" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904631795?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904631795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2891151101444811711"><b>There's something <u>so special</u> about this series.</b><br/><br/>I'm not going to lie, it's a bit complicated. It takes its sweet time revealing bits and pieces of itself to the reader. The magic isn't always intuitive, the characters' motivations aren't always laid out nicely and neatly. <b>But it's always fascinating and keeps me asking questions.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>It's not a series I would recommend for those of us without patience.</i>
</b><br/><br/>It's unique second person point of view is, again, one of the best uses of this perspective I hav</span>
  <span id="freeText2891151101444811711" style="display:none"><b>There's something <u>so special</u> about this series.</b><br /><br />I'm not going to lie, it's a bit complicated. It takes its sweet time revealing bits and pieces of itself to the reader. The magic isn't always intuitive, the characters' motivations aren't always laid out nicely and neatly. <b>But it's always fascinating and keeps me asking questions.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>It's not a series I would recommend for those of us without patience.</i>
</b><br /><br />It's unique second person point of view is, again, one of the best uses of this perspective I have ever seen. <u>It gives you a profound sense of revelation to experience the journey this way.</u><br /><br />This narrative choice is only complimented by Jemisin's writing style. While reading this series I felt completely rapt, transported directly into this cruel and dying world. <b>It's a startling and enchanting experience.</b> <br /><br />Can I also just say how much I <b>
  <i>love the diversity in this series.</i>
</b> There is so much here that it's difficult to even list it all! Diversity is <u>severely lacking</u> in High Fantasy and Science Fiction, and it's just so refreshing to see so much representation. <br /><br />If I ever hear someone say <i>"But it's hard for me to include diversity in my novel!"</i> then I will absolutely point them in the direction of this series because the inclusivity is <u>flawless.</u><br /><br />I really only had <u>two noteworthy</u> issues with this installment:<br /><br />1. I feel as though the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> is <b>more compelling</b> for a specific reason. There was a very distinctive aspect of the storytelling that, because of events from the first novel, could not be present in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26228034.The_Obelisk_Gate__The_Broken_Earth___2_" title="The Obelisk Gate (The Broken Earth, #2) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Obelisk Gate</a>.<br /><br />This aspect is one of the reasons I <i>adore</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> so much, and while Jemisin works incredibly well with where she took her story, it's difficult not to make comparisons.<br /><br />2. This book <b>feels</b> like a middle book. It's great, but not as great as its predecessor. It's packed with more information and less action than the first, but I get the feeling it needed to be that way in order to set up events that will take place in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31817749.The_Stone_Sky__The_Broken_Earth___3_" title="The Stone Sky (The Broken Earth, #3) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stone Sky</a>. <br /><br />Despite these minor issues, I was still incredibly engaged in this story &amp; I'm honestly devastated thinking about waiting until August to see it through. This series is unlike other fantasy series that I have read in the past, and I'm so thrilled to see how it concludes!<br /><br /><i><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/34-mary-s-reviews/760-theobeliskgate" rel="nofollow noopener">This review</a> and other reviews of mine can be found on <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Nest</a>!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2891151101444811711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2025939755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2025939755" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2025939755?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025939755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3223345294052534901"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The way of the world isn’t the strong devouring the weak, but the weak deceiving and poisoning and whispering in the ears of the strong until they become weak, too.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>So... that was good. That was really, really good.<br/><br/>I think… I talked about what makes this series special thematically a lot in my review for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946460674' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fifth Season.</a> But I genuinely think the core of this series, the thing that makes it so impactful, is how it talks about oppression. I was really looking at orogeny in book one </span>
  <span id="freeText3223345294052534901" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The way of the world isn’t the strong devouring the weak, but the weak deceiving and poisoning and whispering in the ears of the strong until they become weak, too.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />So... that was good. That was really, really good.<br /><br />I think… I talked about what makes this series special thematically a lot in my review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946460674" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season.</a> But I genuinely think the core of this series, the thing that makes it so impactful, is how it talks about oppression. I was really looking at orogeny in book one as a metaphor for racism, which it <i>is</i>, but I think it also functions as a metaphor for homophobia. There are several scenes here with Nassun &amp; Gija that are basically word-for-word homophobia. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It's not hate that you're seeing. Hate requires emotion. What this woman has simply done is realize that you are a rogga, and decide that you aren't a person, just like that.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />In this book, we get povs from three characters; Essun, Nassun, and Schaffa. <br />➽Essun - Listen, Essun is my wife. I love how mentally strong she is, I love her drily sarcastic inner monologue. I love that she’s written in second person and it somehow works for me. [Oh, and I love that we know who the first-person narrator of this part of her story is.]<br />➽Nassun - Essun’s daughter, who we didn’t get much of in book one, but who I absolutely <i>love</i>. Her character development is so great; I love how she’s forced to learn to be manipulative, to play the emotions of her father and so many others.<br />➽Schaffa - a villain from the first book who is <i>weirdly</i> sympathetic here. I actually think there’s a lot of talent in creating a villain here who is still the villain, decidedly not an antihero, but gains some of your sympathy? God, I like… despised this character in book one and now I’m out here being kind of emo, but still hating him, and it’s really great. <br /><br />One thing that <i>really</i> shocked me here is how invested I got in like, every side character? I sort of jokingly described this book on my twitter as Essun And Her Gay Friends Try To Survive The Apocalypse They Caused and I was kidding but also, am I wrong? There’s Tonkee, a trans lesbian icon and one of the funniest and most endearing characters in this book. There’s Hoa, who is probably not even human and I kind of love him. [He’s so sweet?] There’s Alabaster, who I’ve talked about a lot and I love to cry. Ykka, a literal icon. Antimony, who I can’t decide how to feel about. So many more.<br /><br />Something I <i>really</i> like about this is that the worldbuilding is super well-thought-out - like, it holds up to really intricate analysis - but still not boring or convoluted. I think sometimes authors can be too fascinated by their own magic systems and not fascinated enough by the characters and plot, but guys, I don’t care about magic systems and I was <i>still</i> not bored by a single moment of this book. N.K. Jemisin is talented at building a compelling world [the only flaw is perhaps the cringeworthily bare map] but focuses on the more compelling parts of the narrative. <br /><br />The problem I really had with this book was that it <i>really</i> feels like a middle book. And this is really concerning, because as the #1 middle book defender. It is my belief that a meh middle book will usually lead to a terrible final book. This is true for every goddamn example of a bad middle book that you will come up with. Divergent? The Fifth Wave? The Maze Runner? If it doesn’t follow this pattern it’s probably because the middle book <i>didn’t</i> suck. So basically. Fear.gif.<br /><br />But, you know, I'm 75% through The Stone Sky, and I figured I might as well post this. Wish me luck!<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3223345294052534901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3557328739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3557328739" />
    <a title="Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70046142-elle"><img alt="Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548160841p2/70046142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3557328739?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle" href="/user/show/70046142-elle">Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3557328739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13206838611902544943"><i>“Being useful to others is not the same thing as being equal.”</i><br/><br/>This series has been the most unexpected but welcome surprise for me this year. I can’t overstate how utterly fantastic N.K. Jemisin’s work is in this trilogy. I don’t know that I’ve read a sci-fi/dystopian/fantasy that better understands the human condition than <i>The Broken Earth</i> trilogy does.<br/><br/>We are back with Essun as she tries to either save or destroy the world, I don’t think anyone is sure which yet. She’s recently reunited with Al</span>
  <span id="freeText13206838611902544943" style="display:none"><i>“Being useful to others is not the same thing as being equal.”</i><br /><br />This series has been the most unexpected but welcome surprise for me this year. I can’t overstate how utterly fantastic N.K. Jemisin’s work is in this trilogy. I don’t know that I’ve read a sci-fi/dystopian/fantasy that better understands the human condition than <i>The Broken Earth</i> trilogy does.<br /><br />We are back with Essun as she tries to either save or destroy the world, I don’t think anyone is sure which yet. She’s recently reunited with Alabaster, albeit not to his normal strength. He still has so much to teach her, but they are running out of time. The world is running out of time. All the characters we met and arrived with in Catstrima are still around, for now, but facing some new challenges. There’s even more exploration of what it means to be an orogene and how the obelisks are connected with their powers.<br /><br />The biggest difference between <i>The Obelisk Gate</i> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> is the inclusion of Nassun’s perspective. She was a character that was very much at the center of Essun’s journey in the first book, but one that we never actually got to meet. Not only do we catch up with what Nassun’s been doing in the mean time, but Jesimin gives us a full replay of what happened to her and her father, Jija, from the horrific event that spurred their departure from Tirimo to present day. But Nassun doesn’t just have to deal with her angry and temperamental father, but another figure, this one from her mother’s past, who’s intentions are difficult to discern. <br /><br />This is definitely a middle-of-a-trilogy book, but that doesn’t mean it still isn’t excellent. It has more character depth and world-building than most other books in a series do combined. The first one was mind-blowing for me, and I think it was better, but I won’t be marking this one down because it didn’t reach that level completely. I still absolutely loved this installment from Jemisin and am having bitter-sweet feelings about finishing this masterclass in story-telling.<br /><br />I don’t really refer to any books as ‘must reads’, but this series is a <b>must read for fantasy/sci-fi fans.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13206838611902544943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3099963994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3099963994" />
    <a title="Always Pouting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting"><img alt="Always Pouting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483476563p2/48650982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3099963994?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28147302-the-obelisk-gate">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3099963994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11478304522384131917">So I read this right after I finished the first one and I read the third one right after. I have to say that I found this to be my favorite out of the three books and the strongest out of the trilogy. Personally I didn't quite like the parts of the book written through second person POV and it felt really weird when it was addressing it directly to the person reading. I think what I enjoyed most about this book was the character development and the complexity brought to the characters we met in </span>
  <span id="freeText11478304522384131917" style="display:none">So I read this right after I finished the first one and I read the third one right after. I have to say that I found this to be my favorite out of the three books and the strongest out of the trilogy. Personally I didn't quite like the parts of the book written through second person POV and it felt really weird when it was addressing it directly to the person reading. I think what I enjoyed most about this book was the character development and the complexity brought to the characters we met in book one. I enjoyed getting more context about the world we're in as well and I really liked that we got to follow Nassun on her own journey. I think a few of the other reviewers said they didn't think this one was as good but I'm not sure why I felt differently. I think it might just be due in part to the fact that we got a lot of the set up out of the way and usually having things being built up feels annoying to me, regardless of the fact that context is necessary especially in fantasy. Yeah but I really enjoyed this, I think its obvious from the fact that I spent over 24 hours just reading to finish the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11478304522384131917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2053973962" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2053973962" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2053973962?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2053973962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15855231150858368450"><b>*** 4.44 ***</b><br/><br/>I did not wait for a buddy read, because after finishing the first book I HAD TO KNOW!!! I engulfed this one in a day and have to say, despite loving the heck out of it, my thirst to KNOW is not quenched... I need the third book right now, but alas, I will have to wait like a good and patient reader and preorder it, so I can have it as soon as it comes out, if not possible to get it earlier. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"..."Life cannot exist without the Earth.Yet there is a not-unsubstantiated chance that li</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText15855231150858368450" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.44 ***</b><br /><br />I did not wait for a buddy read, because after finishing the first book I HAD TO KNOW!!! I engulfed this one in a day and have to say, despite loving the heck out of it, my thirst to KNOW is not quenched... I need the third book right now, but alas, I will have to wait like a good and patient reader and preorder it, so I can have it as soon as it comes out, if not possible to get it earlier. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."Life cannot exist without the Earth.Yet there is a not-unsubstantiated chance that life will win its war, and destroy the Earth. We’ve come close a few times.<br />That can’t happen. We cannot be permitted to win."..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Lets get the most obvious things out of the way. The strength of this book, and the first one for that matter, is the world and character building. Not only solid, not only meticulous, not only imaginative, but also so well chiseled within the reality of the World, that as weird and foreign as it should seem to us, we feel like a part of the creatures who are trying to survive within this dying Earth. You feel the hopes, and dreams, and despair, even at times understand the prejudices, because you wonder if you wouldn't be one of those who in the face of extermination, might put their life and their fears above those of others, just as desperate as you. I could feel the dying of green nature around, the sand and ash under my feet and in the air, the heat, scolding and burning away my fat... I was aware of my own age and disabilities, sharpening my understanding that unless my brain does not compensate for them, I would be one of the first left outside of the comms. I could feel the stifling humidity and smell the purification and copper of bodily fluids... And I saw the petrified chunks of humans, or not, here and there among the boiling bugs. This is how real it all felt. This is how brilliant the writing is! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“But if you stay, no part of this comm gets to decide that any part of this comm is expendable. No voting on who gets to be people.”...“Being useful to others is not the same thing as being equal.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />We have our exquisitely developed main characters of Essun and her daughter Nassun, and Alabaster, all of them powerful Orogenes, as well as the Guardian Schaffa, who is turning out to be a catalyst for both mother and child... There are also the ever hanging around Stone-Eaters, and my favorite Hoa, the one I wish we get more page time with, because he is written in a manner to steal and break your heart! We get a story about the apocalyptic event which lead to the Seasons in first place, and I have to gloat a bit and say that I had that one figured out in the last book:):):) We also started noticing the distinctions between erogeny and magic, and their role in this book was awesomely powerful! The battle of survival kicks up a notch, since the resources are getting depleted as time goes and hope for future sustainable renewal is none existent. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Love is no inoculation against murder.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Amid the epic battle of a world and its inhabitants to survive, we also witness a very heart-wrenching conflict of a family torn by secrets and murder. Jija has taken his daughter, his one child left, his daddy's girl Nassun, up North in order to find a "cure" for her Orogeny. Nassun loves her dad and has grown to hate her mother, since she is the one who had told her to hide her talent and gave her lessons in control with the same brutality she herself was raised with. In Nassun's eyes this was abuse, this was something she believed her mother did just to hurt her, with no particular justification or sense of love. She is happy to be away from the strict and demanding matriarch. Meanwhile, Essun is frantically searching for her beloved daughter, the one that is so much like her, the one she has been very hard on, because the fear of loosing her had made her weigh the positives of cruelty against the negatives being gentle and her girl hurting someone by mistake, not understanding her own power, and getting lynched because of it. Which one of those lose-lose situations makes her a monster deserving her child's hatred? I personally thing that although harsh and cruel, Essun did the right thing, refusing to make a victim out of her daughter. Hopefully, in the process of making her strong, she did not create a monster... <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Given a choice between death and the barest possibility of acceptance, they were desperate, and we used that. We made them desperate.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />I will not delve into the plot itself, because that is the joy of reading the book - discovering it for yourself!!! I do have to say that it was a non-stop, exciting and riveting, at times devastating, at times adrenaline-inducing, but always poignant and ethically challenging. I loved it! It is a set-up book for what I hope will be a bang of a finish, and I only have to wait one more month for it!!! My impatience will have to read something else in order not to drive me insane in the meantime:):):) <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“All that stuff about Father Earth, it's just stories to explain what's wrong with the world. Like those weird cults that crop up from time to time. I heard of one that asks an old man in the sky to keep them alive every time they go to sleep. People need to believe there's more to the world than there is.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy reading and many more wonderful books to come!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15855231150858368450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1394380152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394380152" />
    <a title="Tess Burton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4098917-tess-burton"><img alt="Tess Burton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593448934p2/4098917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1394380152?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tess Burton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tess Burton" href="/user/show/4098917-tess-burton">Tess Burton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=didnt-meet-expectations">didnt-meet-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=dystopia-or-apocalyptic">dystopia-or-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4098917-tess-burton?shelf=antihero">antihero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394380152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2626401829574387320">To summarize, it seems even the best authors can fall victim to Middle Book Syndrome.<br/><br/>I still adore N.K. Jemisin, I still think she's a goddess. <em>The Obelisk Gate</em> just didn't do it for me. The first book in this series, <em>The Fifth Season</em>, was just so exciting. It was filled with incredible world-building and a well-paced journey with a complex and likable heroine. But whereas <em>The Fifth Season</em> was probably 70% backstory, I should really have known this installment would focus more on the present.<br/><br/>The</span>
  <span id="freeText2626401829574387320" style="display:none">To summarize, it seems even the best authors can fall victim to Middle Book Syndrome.<br /><br />I still adore N.K. Jemisin, I still think she's a goddess. <em>The Obelisk Gate</em> just didn't do it for me. The first book in this series, <em>The Fifth Season</em>, was just so exciting. It was filled with incredible world-building and a well-paced journey with a complex and likable heroine. But whereas <em>The Fifth Season</em> was probably 70% backstory, I should really have known this installment would focus more on the present.<br /><br />The first half of the book was (comparatively) dull as mud. Nothing of much interest happens to Essun, she appeared stagnant and incapable. We got more about Nassun, Essun's daughter, and her life-changing journey after the beginning of the latest apocalypse. Ultimately, she was interesting, but not for a long while.<br /><br />By the time things really started happening, I had already given into my boredom. I really wasn't invested, and all I was really hoping for was more of Schaffa's backstory. He had quickly become the most intriguing character, as my love for Essun kind of waned.<br /><br />I'm still going to read the final installment of this trilogy, but I hope the pacing improves in the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2626401829574387320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3294947882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11685861884685453300"><a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/09/20/the-obelisk-gate-the-stone-sky-reviews/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“It’s not hate that you’re seeing. Hate requires emotion. What this woman has simply done is realize that you are a rogga, and decide that you aren’t a person, just like that.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><b>You, Surprised</b><br/><br/>You are disappointed, you liked book 1. You actually had a gut feeling that book 2 will not be as good which made you keep putting reading it off. Your instinct seems right. You actually was bored while reading the book and confuse</span>
  <span id="freeText11685861884685453300" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/09/20/the-obelisk-gate-the-stone-sky-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“It’s not hate that you’re seeing. Hate requires emotion. What this woman has simply done is realize that you are a rogga, and decide that you aren’t a person, just like that.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 stars</b><br /><br /><b>You, Surprised</b><br /><br />You are disappointed, you liked book 1. You actually had a gut feeling that book 2 will not be as good which made you keep putting reading it off. Your instinct seems right. You actually was bored while reading the book and confused and the goal became finishing it rather than enjoying it. That's a bad sign. You are not happy but you are still going to continue the series to see if it gets better.<br /><br />This is how this review ends, not with a bang but a whimper...<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11685861884685453300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
